## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t). Nonlinearity introduces higher-order terms in x and v beyond the simple linear oscillator.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 - c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on amplitude)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric excitation)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- General driven damped nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * (1 - c3 * x**2) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (comprehensive nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well, preserving spatial symmetry of oscillation
- Even-power restoring terms (x²) → asymmetric potential, indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms with position modulation (v·x², v·(1-x²)) → amplitude-dependent damping/self-excitation (limit cycles)
- Cubic restoring term sign: positive c1 in x³ → hardening spring (frequency increases with amplitude); negative → softening spring
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c·t) or sin(c·t) → external periodic driving or parametric excitation
- Product terms x·v → energy-exchange coupling between kinetic and potential degrees of freedom
- Odd-power velocity terms (v³) → nonlinear drag, relevant at high velocities
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, energy conservation or dissipation without external input

# Analysis

## Ground Truth Expression

The GT is:
$$f(x,t,v) = -3.42786x(0.034998|v|^{1/3} + 1) + 0.10030\sin(t) - 0.88849\sin(v)$$

Expanding:
$$f = -3.42786x - 0.11997x|v|^{1/3} + 0.10030\sin(t) - 0.88849\sin(v)$$

Key features:
1. A term proportional to $x$ (linear in $x$)
2. A term proportional to $x|v|^{1/3}$ (nonlinear coupling with absolute value)
3. $\sin(t)$ term
4. $\sin(v)$ term (note: $\sin(v)$, not a polynomial in $v$)

The $\sin(v)$ term is crucial - it cannot be represented as a polynomial in $v$. Let me check if any candidate can accommodate this.

## Critical Observation

The GT contains $\sin(v)$, which is a transcendental function of $v$. None of the candidates contain $\sin(v)$. Most candidates use polynomial terms in $v$ (like $v$, $v^3$, $v^2 x$, etc.) and trigonometric functions only of $t$.

For the $\sin(v)$ term, we can write its Taylor expansion: $\sin(v) \approx v - v^3/6 + v^5/120 - ...$

So $-0.88849\sin(v) \approx -0.88849v + 0.14808v^3 - ...$

The candidates all have terms $c_1 v + c_2 v^3$, which can approximate the first two terms of the Taylor expansion, but cannot exactly match $\sin(v)$ for all $v$.

Similarly, the GT has $x|v|^{1/3}$, which involves an absolute value and fractional power. This cannot be exactly represented by polynomial terms in $v$ and $x$.

Since the task asks for **mathematical equivalence** (not approximation), and:
- $\sin(v)$ cannot be expressed as any finite polynomial in $v$
- $x|v|^{1/3}$ cannot be expressed as any finite polynomial combination of $x$ and $v$

No candidate with only polynomial terms in $v$ can exactly match the GT.

Let me check if any candidate has non-polynomial terms in $v$:
- Candidate 1: has $x\exp(c_9 v^2)$ - this is exponential in $v^2$, not equivalent to $|v|^{1/3}$ or $\sin(v)$
- Candidate 21: has $v\exp(c_9 x^2)$ - exponential in $x^2$
- Candidate 50: has $x\exp(c_8 x^2)$ - exponential in $x^2$
- Candidate 22: has $\log(c_9 x^2 + 1)$ - logarithmic in $x$

None of these non-polynomial terms involve the right functional forms to match $\sin(v)$ or $|v|^{1/3}x$.

Even candidates with $\cos(c_4 t + c_5\sin(c_6 t + c_7))$ (candidates 35, 39-43, 45-46) only have more complex time-dependence, not $v$-dependence.

## Conclusion

The GT contains two terms that no candidate can replicate:
1. $\sin(v)$ - a transcendental function of $v$
2. $x|v|^{1/3}$ - involves absolute value and fractional power of $v$

No candidate formula contains $\sin(v)$ or $|v|^{1/3}$ or any equivalent non-polynomial function of $v$ that could match these terms. Therefore, no candidate can be mathematically equivalent to the GT for any choice of constants.
